    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer12820799162160448599">Sixteen-year-old physics nerd Aysel is obsessed with plotting her own death. With a mother who can barely look at her without wincing, classmates who whisper behind her back, and a father whose violent crime rocked her small town, Aysel is ready to turn her potential energy into nothingness.<br/><br/>There’s only one problem: she’s not sure she has the courage to do it alone. But on</span>
  <span id="freeText12820799162160448599" style="display:none">Sixteen-year-old physics nerd Aysel is obsessed with plotting her own death. With a mother who can barely look at her without wincing, classmates who whisper behind her back, and a father whose violent crime rocked her small town, Aysel is ready to turn her potential energy into nothingness.<br /><br />There’s only one problem: she’s not sure she has the courage to do it alone. But once she discovers a website with a section called Suicide Partners, Aysel’s convinced she’s found her solution: a teen boy with the username FrozenRobot (aka Roman) who’s haunted by a family tragedy is looking for a partner. <br /><br />Even though Aysel and Roman have nothing in common, they slowly start to fill in each other’s broken lives. But as their suicide pact becomes more concrete, Aysel begins to question whether she really wants to go through with it. Ultimately, she must choose between wanting to die or trying to convince Roman to live so they can discover the potential of their energy together. Except that Roman may not be so easy to convince.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12820799162160448599" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    No they don't die. Not even one of them. Not like in ALL THE BRIGHT PLACES. I get why you wanted to know. I wanted to too. I guess it kind of defeats <a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    No they don't die. Not even one of them. Not like in ALL THE BRIGHT PLACES. I get why you wanted to know. I wanted to too. I guess it kind of defeats the point a little but I just didn't want to bawl my eyes out like in ATBP. So... no. You'll be happy with the ending. Promise, <br /><br />-A<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1221529206?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jesse (JesseTheReader)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jesse (JesseTheReader)" href="/user/show/8114361-jesse-jessethereader">Jesse (JesseTheReader)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1221529206" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12336840255291689970"><b>trigger warning for suicide with this book. </b><br/>Where do I even begin? This story was at times hard to read, not because it was bad (it was AMAZING), but because it was so dark. I wanted to dive into this book and lead the characters in a different direction. I'm struggling finding words to express my feelings for this book. I'll just simply say, I loved it. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_972734222" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/972734222" />
    <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair"><img alt="Steph Sinclair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457555690p2/4642710.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/972734222?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steph Sinclair" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair">Steph Sinclair</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062324672" href="/book/show/22328549-my-heart-and-other-black-holes">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">not depressed teens</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=mental-health">mental-health</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=disappointment">disappointment</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2015-release">2015-release</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=harpercollins">harpercollins</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=no-just-no">no-just-no</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=youve-got-to-be-kidding-me">youve-got-to-be-kidding-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=tough-issues">tough-issues</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=could-have-been-better">could-have-been-better</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer972734222" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6790089177331086093">I came really close to DNFing this book at 96% on principle alone because I was fed one thing in the beginning of the novel, only to be force fed something entirely different by the end. <em>My Heart and Other Black Holes</em> had so much potential--a lot of novel accurately described what it feels like to be depressed. So I was expecting a novel about discovering yourself, overcoming depression and finding something to live for. I was excited for it because it's a topic that needs more awareness and und</span>
  <span id="freeText6790089177331086093" style="display:none">I came really close to DNFing this book at 96% on principle alone because I was fed one thing in the beginning of the novel, only to be force fed something entirely different by the end. <em>My Heart and Other Black Holes</em> had so much potential--a lot of novel accurately described what it feels like to be depressed. So I was expecting a novel about discovering yourself, overcoming depression and finding something to live for. I was excited for it because it's a topic that needs more awareness and understanding. And for about 60% of the book, I got just that, but somewhere along the way, <em>My Heart and Other Black Holes</em> got ridiculously lost and confused. What happened?<br /><br /><strong>Be warned: Unhidden spoilers and very personal feelings ahead.<br /></strong><br /><br />Aysel is battling depression in the aftermath of a public tragedy that befell her family. Her father murdered their small town's star athlete, and as a result Aysel carries a burden of guilt of the incident. There's also a part of her that wonders if she, too, will end up like her father. She suffers in silence, never allowing anyone in, even former friends that stood by her after the tragedy, convincing herself that it's for their benefit to not be associated with her. In fact, she's convinced her own mother and siblings would be better off without her, too, going as far to remind her younger sister that they are half-siblings whenever she can.<br /><br />Her pain is real, and as someone who has suffered from depression and social isolation for the past 7 years and anxiety issues for longer than I can remember, I could relate to the "black slug" that she continues to reference throughout the novel. Depression is a hard thing to describe to someone who has never experienced it, and until I personally dealt with it, I can honestly say that I had no idea. Even to this day, I find it difficult to fully explain it to my husband who, bless his little heart, tries his very best to be as understanding as humanly possible. Fully understanding would involve him feeling this heavy thing and I wouldn't wish that on my worst enemy, let alone him. But it's great that he listens and it's even better that he's there and has that <em>want</em> to understand. So as I was reading, I found little quotes that perfectly described feelings that I've felt and I read them out loud to him.<br /><blockquote>Depression is like a heaviness that you can't ever escape. It crushes down on you, making even the smallest things like tying your shoes or chewing on toast seem like a twenty-mile hike uphill. Depression is a part of you; it's in your bones and your blood. If I know anything about it, this is what I know: It's impossible to escape.</blockquote><br />Aysel's voice felt very true to her situation and worked well with a topic as heavy as this. It never felt like it needed more or less of that <em>something </em>for me to connect with what Aysel was saying because I completely understood where she was coming from. I've been there; I'm still there.<br /><blockquote>What people never understand is that depression isn't about the outside; it's about the inside. Something inside me is wrong. Sure, there are things in my life that make me feel alone, but nothing makes me feel more isolated and terrified than my own voice in my head.</blockquote><br />I also loved how Roman described how he felt about missing his little sister because it reminds me of how I feel when I think of my little brother.<br /><blockquote>The hardest moments are when I miss her in the future.</blockquote><br />After my brother passed away, for a long time, I had moments where it was like a part of my mind was still in denial. I'd see a commercial and absentmindedly think, "Oh man, wait till I tell Steve about this" and then remember that I couldn't do that and have a long cry. Sometimes I still do that and it hurts so much because life has gone on without him, I've gone on without him, and that feels wrong and unfair. So I completely related to Roman's grief of losing a sibling. And strangely, even though, this book made me remember certain feelings, it never depressed me. It was more like a bunch of "I know that feel, bro" moments while reading.<br /><br />This is where Warga excels in <em>My Heart and Other Black Holes</em> and why the first 50% is so dead on. It's also why I said I was loving it around that marker.<br /><br /><strong>Unfortunately, it went downhill from there.</strong><br /><br />Sometimes I just want to have a heart to heart with the book I'm reading. I want to invite it to tea and a spot on my comfy couch and tell them one thing: Look, <strong>I know you're a YA novel, but you don't always have to have a romance.</strong><br /><br />With the introduction to Roman, a boy who Aysel finds on a Suicide Partners forum, we get romance. Now, this is partly my fault, because if I actually read blurbs like a normal person before starting a book, I would have seen this part and ran the other way:<br /><blockquote>
  Even though Aysel and Roman have nothing in common, they slowly start to fill in each others' broken lives. But as their suicide pact becomes more concrete, Aysel begins to question whether she really wants to go through with it. Ultimately, she must choose between wanting to die or trying to convince Roman to live so they can discover the potential of their energy together.
</blockquote><br />This is problematic for me on so many levels.<br /><br /><strong>1. Romanticization</strong><br /><br />I want to make this clear: <strong>I am not saying any of this is authorial intent.</strong> As soon as you introduce teenage romance to a a topic as heavy as this, you run this risk of it being romanticized. I saw moments of this when Roman started saying things like:<br /><blockquote>"You're you. You get it. you get all of it. And you're sad like me, and screwed up as that is, it's pretty beautiful." He reaches over and brushes his hand across my face, touching my hair. "You're like a gray sky. You're beautiful, even though you don't want to be."</blockquote><br />This gave me pause because one of the reasons why Roman liked Aysel was because she was depressed and wanted to kill herself. But I was willing to let this go because at this point it seemed like only Roman had these twisted feelings while Aysel was bothered by it.<br /><blockquote>But he was wrong. It's not that I don't want to be. But I never wanted to be beautiful because I was sad. FrozenRobot of all people should know that there is nothing beautiful or endearing or glamorous about sadness. Sadness is only ugly, and anyone who thinks otherwise doesn't get it.</blockquote><br />I was further bothered when other characters started pairing the couple off, telling them they looked cute together. But I still had hope because Aysel hadn't completely lost her grip on reality... yet.<br /><blockquote>If I have a boyfriend, his name is Death. And I'm pretty sure Roman is in love with him, too. It's like a love triangle gone wrong. Or maybe it's a love triangle gone right: we both get the guy on April 7.</blockquote><br />I would have much preferred if the romance was left completely out. What Aysel needed was understanding and a person she could talk to. If there's one thing I've learned about depression, it's that it can't be conquered alone. Having someone who can relate to your own situation, who knows exactly how you're feeling, without having to spell it out to them, is invaluable. I have a person like that in my life and she is amazing and thoughtful and strong and she's probably reading this review right now, wondering if I'm talking about her. (Yes, it's you, Kat.) I literally don't know what I'd do if I had never met her. She is my person. So I get the need for her to connect to someone. It does help, but this needed to be accomplished without romanticizing the situation and it wasn't.<br /><br />It's basically the same way I felt about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11870085-the-fault-in-our-stars?ac=1" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>The Fault in Our Stars</em>
</a>: great idea, but the romance distracted from the central conflict and somehow made it all about their love. (Which is why I've been saying that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12700353-me-and-earl-and-the-dying-girl?ac=1" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>Me, Earl and the Dying Girl</em>
</a> is a much better alternative to <em>The Fault in Our Stars</em>.) <strong>Introducing this romance cheapened the story and the connection I thought I had to the characters.</strong> All of a sudden Roman is kissing Aysel, telling her how he wishes things could be different for them in another universe, but that she better not flake out on him come April 7th, that it changes nothing. It went from Aysel overcoming her demons and finding a reason to live to I'm in love with Roman, but he still wants to kill himself, let me save him with the new found love in my heart. And just no.<br /><br /><strong>2. Love is the Cure-All</strong><br /><br />There comes a point in <em>My Heart and Other Black Holes</em> where Aysel has this AH-HA moment (ironically, sometime after kissing Roman--gag me) and decides she really doesn't want to die after all. Apparently, all it took was someone telling her it wasn't her fault for what her father did and she magically gets over her depression. Why? Because someone she has grown to care about accepted her and changed her in less than a month. <strong>There was way too much change in her attitude and outlook on life and not enough catalyst to justify it.</strong> That deeply bothered me.<br /><br />I understand that she made a commitment to be stronger than her sadness, it was a great start. But depression is more than just sadness and is not something you can just decide to "get over" one day, especially if you've been suffering for years and are at the point where you are contemplating suicide. If the word "sad" were a bucket, depression would overflow it ten times over. Being depressed isn't a choice, it's a disease, a war within yourself. One where everyday is its own battle. It's not something that can be overcome by love alone. As awesome as that sounds, it's unrealistic.<br /><br /><strong>3. Loose Ends</strong><br /><br />Aysel did have people in her life who was trying to reach out to her before Roman entered into the picture. Instead of the reader seeing Aysel get the closure she's been desperately craving, we get Aysel worried over Roman and <em>his</em> suicide attempt. Of course, this is why the romance felt so out of place and inappropriate to me: it monopolized the central conflict--Aysel's battle--and morphed into it being about Aysel saving Roman with love.<br /><br />What I wanted was more closure with Aysel and her family. I was hoping we'd get to see them visiting her dad, finally letting her sister Georgia into her life, reconnecting with her mother, seeing a doctor for her problems. Asyel's broken family life was one of the biggest things that led to her depression and I was <em>very</em> disappointed to see this not addressed in the end. (Side note: I am scratching my head at Aysel's mother's decision making. She willingly left her daughter with her father knowing that he had violent tendencies? Never reached out to her further when she got remarried and had more kids? And then she was shocked to learn about her depression? Shocked that Aysel didn't come to her? HUH?)<br /><br />By that time I was at 96% of the novel, I wanted to rage quit because I knew the book couldn't pull off what I needed it to. I was right because the final scene is full of Roman in the hospital after his failed suicide attempt and Aysel there confessing her love.<br /><blockquote>
  
    "Because loving you saved me. It's made me see myself differently, see the world differently. I owe you everything for that."
  
</blockquote><br />So much no.<br /><br /><em>My Heart and Other Black Holes</em> could have been amazing. It could have been the book I'd recommend to really help people understand what it feels like to be depressed. The descriptions of grief were spot on and genuine. But the glamorized-suicidal-romantic-teen-love-fest killed any hope of redemption. I love a hope-filled story as much as the next person, and oh how I wish depression could just be cured with a little bit of love. I wish loving my husband and kids and them loving me in return could fix me. <strong>Love is a lot of things, but it is not a magic pill.</strong> This is real life, and real life is a lot more complicated and messy than that. What <em>My Heart and Other Black Holes</em> does do is give off a <em>false</em> hope with the road it took to achieving it almost impossible to attain. And <em>that</em>, frankly, depresses the hell out of me.<br /><br />ARC provided by publisher in exchange for an honest review. <br /><br />More reviews and other fantastical things at <a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Cuddlebuggery</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6790089177331086093" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1054899474" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1054899474" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1054899474?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780062324696" href="/book/show/22308720-my-heart-and-other-black-holes">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1054899474" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4346039985049414910"><i>Does a dead body still have potential energy or does it get transferred into something else? Can potential energy just evaporate into nothingness? That’s the question I don’t know the answer to. That’s the question that haunts me.</i><br/><br/><b>3 1/2 stars.</b> This book was pretty much perfect until the big thing that made it not so perfect anymore. However, I still think it's a clever, addicting, sensitive, honest and insightful story about depression, especially in the beginning. It follows the pattern of other</span>
  <span id="freeText4346039985049414910" style="display:none"><i>Does a dead body still have potential energy or does it get transferred into something else? Can potential energy just evaporate into nothingness? That’s the question I don’t know the answer to. That’s the question that haunts me.</i><br /><br /><b>3 1/2 stars.</b> This book was pretty much perfect until the big thing that made it not so perfect anymore. However, I still think it's a clever, addicting, sensitive, honest and insightful story about depression, especially in the beginning. It follows the pattern of other popular books that I didn't enjoy so much - like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11870085.The_Fault_in_Our_Stars" title="The Fault in Our Stars by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fault in Our Stars</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18460392.All_the_Bright_Places" title="All the Bright Places by Jennifer Niven" rel="nofollow noopener">All the Bright Places</a> - but the characters felt more real and less annoyingly pretentious. Plus, <b>I loved the philosophy/physics angle.</b><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18336965.My_Heart_and_Other_Black_Holes" title="My Heart and Other Black Holes by Jasmine Warga" rel="nofollow noopener">My Heart and Other Black Holes</a> starts very well. Having suffered with depression at times in my life and seen my mother deal with it too, I can completely relate to Aysel's descriptions of her sadness and inner struggle. Warga apparently wrote this book after the death of her close friend, in order to manage her own emotions and I think it's evident that she understands her subject. Like how the worst of it happens inside of you:<br /><br /><i>
  <b>What people never understand is that depression isn’t about the outside; it’s about the inside. Something inside me is wrong. Sure, there are things in my life that make me feel alone, but nothing makes me feel more isolated and terrified than my own voice in my head.</b>
</i><br /><br />And the wish to be invisible that sometimes borders on agoraphobia:<br /><br /><i>
  <b>In these moments, it always feels like my skin is too thin, like everyone can see right inside me, can see my empty and dark insides.</b>
</i><br /><br />When Aysel decides she needs a suicide partner to finally put an end to her misery, she meets up with Roman. Both of them are very different and very realistic. Aysel might be a really smart physics nerd, but her "voice" feels like that of a real person; a real teenager. And Roman is proof that not all depression sufferers are nerdy outsiders and emos. I also really enjoyed the conversation between them - both the serious discussions and the darkly comic aspects.<br /><br />I wondered how the physics theme was going to play into the story and was skeptical about whether I'd like it. As it turns out, I did. I thought the weaving together of philosophy and physics was really interesting. The question about what happens to us when we die is an old one, but I found this take on it refreshing - <b>if energy cannot disappear but can only be transferred, what happens to our energy when we die?</b><br /><br />My issue with this book started during the last 25%. Warga had built up a strong novel with strong characters who, though bitter, were extremely likable. She'd brought depression, death, life, philosophy and science to the table in an intriguing blend... and then Aysel, um, recovers.<br /><br />I don't know how else to explain it. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Aysel finally admits she has feelings for Rowan and suddenly, overnight, it's like the depression has started to be washed away:<br /><br /><i><b>He’s no longer the person I want to die with; he’s the person I want to be alive with.</b></i><br /><br />I find this to be many things - lazy, untruthful, even a damaging message. Depression is not something that can be cured overnight. As Aysel noted earlier, it's far more to do with the inner illness than the outer circumstances. I wouldn't go so far as to portray this as a "love cures all" book - personally, I didn't even think it was very romancey - but it completely misrepresents depression and suicidal thinking by suggesting that someone can flick a switch in their brain and decide to be happy and alive. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I don't like that suggestion and I needed it to be noted. But I still believe this is a good book. Enjoyable, dark, but funny too. Clever and interesting. I just wish the last 25% had been stronger.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="http://mycountryheart.co.uk/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4346039985049414910" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_796474513" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/796474513" />
    <a title="Becky Albertalli" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26763429-becky-albertalli"><img alt="Becky Albertalli" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1392414750p2/26763429.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/796474513?book_show_action=true">Dec 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky Albertalli" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky Albertalli" href="/user/show/26763429-becky-albertalli">Becky Albertalli</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer796474513" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18082423504003578091">I don't even know where to begin. This is such a special, weird, complicated, beautiful book. I'm a clinical psychologist who spent several years doing therapy almost exclusively with kids and teenagers. This is the book I wish my clients could have read. Aysel's voice is vivid and sad and quietly snarky - she's just so messy and real. She flips the switch from heartbreaking to hilarious in the span of a paragraph. She's sullen and brilliant and frustrating and gorgeously imperfect. Warga nailed</span>
  <span id="freeText18082423504003578091" style="display:none">I don't even know where to begin. This is such a special, weird, complicated, beautiful book. I'm a clinical psychologist who spent several years doing therapy almost exclusively with kids and teenagers. This is the book I wish my clients could have read. Aysel's voice is vivid and sad and quietly snarky - she's just so messy and real. She flips the switch from heartbreaking to hilarious in the span of a paragraph. She's sullen and brilliant and frustrating and gorgeously imperfect. Warga nailed her portrayal of clinical depression, but even more so, she created an achingly familiar, completely realistic teenage character who isn't defined by diagnostic labels. And then she shows us all the messy, dark stuff that truly is a part of reality for so many kids. I think it's so difficult and terrifying to talk about suicidality in a way that connects with the lived experience of these teens. Warga goes there, fearlessly - and I think this authenticity is so sorely needed. </span>
  <a data-text-id="18082423504003578091" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2176918136" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2176918136?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Charlotte May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Charlotte May" href="/user/show/14002983-charlotte-may">Charlotte May</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781444791532" href="/book/show/23301770-my-heart-and-other-black-holes">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=tear-jerker">tear-jerker</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=contemporary-recent">contemporary-recent</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=illness-mental-terminal">illness-mental-terminal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=sisters">sisters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2176918136" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8734145820953795716">3.5 stars ⭐️ <br/><br/><i> “Sometimes I wonder if my heart is like a black hole - it’s so dense that there’s no room for light, but that doesn’t mean it can’t still suck me in.” </i><br/><br/>This was an honest look into teenage suicide. Aysel and Roman meet on an online forum designed for people to find ‘suicide partners’, a person they plan to commit suicide with. <br/>It took a while for me to like the main characters, it seems I’m that way with all characters - I can never like someone immediately. After a few chapters I b</span>
  <span id="freeText8734145820953795716" style="display:none">3.5 stars ⭐️ <br /><br /><i> “Sometimes I wonder if my heart is like a black hole - it’s so dense that there’s no room for light, but that doesn’t mean it can’t still suck me in.” </i><br /><br />This was an honest look into teenage suicide. Aysel and Roman meet on an online forum designed for people to find ‘suicide partners’, a person they plan to commit suicide with. <br />It took a while for me to like the main characters, it seems I’m that way with all characters - I can never like someone immediately. After a few chapters I began to understand their personalities. <br /><br /><i> “This must be a sign from the universe - if the only time you get lucky is when you’re planning your suicide, it’s definitely time to go.” </i><br /><br />We follow Aysel and Roman as they makes their plans, and we learn about their histories and why they both want to die. Earlier this year I read <i> All The Bright Places </i> and it’s hard not to compare the two as they have such similar themes. I have to say though I think I preferred ATBP over this one as it seems to push the idea that falling in love cures your sadness; which just isn’t the case. <br /><br />However, I very much felt the pain of both the characters. They had both gone through very traumatic situations and their isolation was overpowering. <br /><br /><i> “It’s like your sadness is so deep and overwhelming that you’re worried it will drown everyone else in your life if you let them too close to it.” </i><br /><br />I enjoyed their different personalities and how they grew closer, I just don’t think it had quite the depth that ATBP had. <br /><br /><i> “There is nothing beautiful or endearing or glamorous about sadness. Sadness is only ugly...that girl he drew, she was beautiful. She had hope. Hope is beautiful.” </i> </span>
  <a data-text-id="8734145820953795716" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/735748979?book_show_action=true">Oct 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Adam Silvera" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Adam Silvera" href="/user/show/4050629-adam-silvera">Adam Silvera</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062324672" href="/book/show/22328549-my-heart-and-other-black-holes">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4050629-adam-silvera?shelf=2015-debuts">2015-debuts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4050629-adam-silvera?shelf=read-in-2014">read-in-2014</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer735748979" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11463780705895938309">I read this book in one sitting, overnight, and I'm sure many others will find themselves sharing in this experience. MY HEART AND OTHER BLACK HOLES is a panoramic novel about existence, and Aysel and Roman's relationship - suicide partners - is an impressive combination of tragic and life-affirming. There's so much more I want to say, but I should STFU now until there are at least ARCs out in the world. </span>

          </span>

<div id="review_971757477" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/971757477" />
    <a title="Sue (Hollywood News Source)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6511257-sue-hollywood-news-source"><img alt="Sue (Hollywood News Source)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586156113p2/6511257.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/971757477?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sue (Hollywood News Source)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sue (Hollywood News Source)" href="/user/show/6511257-sue-hollywood-news-source">Sue (Hollywood News Source)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6511257-sue-hollywood-news-source?shelf=edelweiss-arc">edelweiss-arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6511257-sue-hollywood-news-source?shelf=characters-of-color">characters-of-color</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6511257-sue-hollywood-news-source?shelf=diverse-books">diverse-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6511257-sue-hollywood-news-source?shelf=fully-freshed-characters">fully-freshed-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6511257-sue-hollywood-news-source?shelf=made-me-cry">made-me-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6511257-sue-hollywood-news-source?shelf=depression-suicide">depression-suicide</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6511257-sue-hollywood-news-source?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6511257-sue-hollywood-news-source?shelf=mental-health">mental-health</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6511257-sue-hollywood-news-source?shelf=interracial-romance">interracial-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6511257-sue-hollywood-news-source?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer971757477" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13111803788933179172"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421777911i/13413762.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Review and playlist posted at <a href='http://youngadulthollywood.com/books/yah-book-review-my-heart-and-other-black-holes-by-jasmine-warga/#.VMAooCvF8rU' rel='nofollow noopener'>Young Adult Hollywood.</a><br/><br/><strong>Disclaimer:</strong> I spent 90% of my time gross sobbing to the point I had to dry my tears, because I couldn't read what I was supposed to be reading.<br/><br/> <blockquote>
<em>“I bet if you cut open my stomach, the black slug of depression would slide out. Guidance counselors always love to say, “Just think positively,” but that’s impossible when you have this thing inside of you, strangling every ounce of happiness you can muster. My body is an efficient happy-thought-killi</em></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText13111803788933179172" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421777911i/13413762.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Review and playlist posted at <a href="http://youngadulthollywood.com/books/yah-book-review-my-heart-and-other-black-holes-by-jasmine-warga/#.VMAooCvF8rU" rel="nofollow noopener">Young Adult Hollywood.</a><br><br><strong>Disclaimer:</strong> I spent 90% of my time gross sobbing to the point I had to dry my tears, because I couldn't read what I was supposed to be reading.<br><br> <blockquote>
<em>“I bet if you cut open my stomach, the black slug of depression would slide out. Guidance counselors always love to say, “Just think positively,” but that’s impossible when you have this thing inside of you, strangling every ounce of happiness you can muster. My body is an efficient happy-thought-killing machine.”</em> </blockquote><br><br>If I could be a book or if there's a story in the world that could describe some part of me as a person, My Heart and Other Black Holes is one of the few titles I would say yeah, this book contains a part of me.<br><br>As far as I could remember, I have always been struggling with depression. It's something that doesn't really go away. Yeah, it comes and goes once in a while, but there is no cure for it. The underlining: it isn't always going to be like that. Eventually, I learned to calm the fire rage inside me. There are some given moments, I realized there are a lot of things worth living for.<br><br>This is why, I feel so grateful to read something that I can identify with. I wish, this book existed when I was in high school. It would have saved me countless of nights crying myself to sleep.<br><br>In My Heart and Other Black Holes, we have Aysel a teenager who is struggling with depression. She wanted to die and has been plotting her own death. But she’s scared, she’s going to flake the last minute. And upon discovering a website called Suicide Partners, she met FrozenRobert who also wanted to die.<br><br>They made a pact to do<em> it</em> together.<br><br>But as they get closer to their deadline date, Aysel begins to question <em>if</em> dying is really worth it.<br><br><strong>The characters and romance:</strong> I love every character from this book. It’s like watching The Red Band Society, there is so much love going on. These bunch of flawed people are authentic and poignant. Be prepared to swoon and cry.<br><br>Contrary to popular belief, My Heart and Other Black Holes is <strong>
  <em>not just a morbid book that will make you shed tears.</em>
</strong> It is also a chock-full story filled with humor and snark.<br><br><strong>Why you should read it:</strong> If you are struggling with depression, or are friends or related to someone who is and you wanted to be enlighten. Then maybe, this book is for you. <br><br>As for someone who constantly grapple with her struggles, I relate to My Heart and Other Black Holes a lot, in some little ways and more. Like all things, it is not a book without flaws and shortcoming.<br><br>Bravo to Jasmine Warga for acknowledging depression is something that is not beautiful. It’s awful, and fucking ugly. It’s something that no one should glamorize.<br><br>My Heart and Other Black Holes is dark, filled with so much hope. It is profoundly moving that dealt with depression realistically.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13111803788933179172" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1514769583" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1514769583" />
    <a title="Christy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11284813-christy"><img alt="Christy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594293998p2/11284813.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1514769583?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christy" href="/user/show/11284813-christy">Christy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11284813-christy?shelf=2016-ya-challenge">2016-ya-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11284813-christy?shelf=2016-audios">2016-audios</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1514769583" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13562188749342832975"><b>4 stars!</b> <br/><br/><a href='http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%209/5359D938-699D-48EC-9987-4A7531795E1C_zps7dw2khqo.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1480070048i/21270615._SY540_.jpg' alt=' photo 5359D938-699D-48EC-9987-4A7531795E1C_zps7dw2khqo.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a> <br/><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“Sometimes I wonder if my heart is like a black hole--it's so dense that there's no room for light, but that doesn't mean it can't still suck me in.”</blockquote>
  </b>
</i> <i>My Heart and Other Black Holes</i> was a unique and at times painful YA read about dealing with depression and guilt. I felt that this story very accurately displayed what it’s like to feel that kind of depression and the desperation that comes along with it. It’s about Asyel and Roman and the battle they’re both facing. <br/><br/>Asyel</span>
  <span id="freeText13562188749342832975" style="display:none"><b>4 stars!</b> <br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%209/5359D938-699D-48EC-9987-4A7531795E1C_zps7dw2khqo.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1480070048i/21270615._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo 5359D938-699D-48EC-9987-4A7531795E1C_zps7dw2khqo.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“Sometimes I wonder if my heart is like a black hole--it's so dense that there's no room for light, but that doesn't mean it can't still suck me in.”</blockquote>
  </b>
</i> <i>My Heart and Other Black Holes</i> was a unique and at times painful YA read about dealing with depression and guilt. I felt that this story very accurately displayed what it’s like to feel that kind of depression and the desperation that comes along with it. It’s about Asyel and Roman and the battle they’re both facing. <br><br>Asyel and Roman don’t have much in common. Besides the fact that they both want to die. This is a heavy story. It tackles sensitive topics and it won’t be for everyone, but it sucked me in from the start. I didn’t want to put it down. And even with all the heavy, there were funny moments, moments that felt hopeful and full of promise. Everyone has something or someone worth living for. Even people in the darkest of places. It’s just finding out what it is.<br><br>  I found this to be an emotional, powerful read with beautifully broken characters and a storyline that made me feel from start to finish! I would recommend this one to lovers of YA looking for something less on the fluffy/fun side. <br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“He’s no longer the person I want to die with; he’s the person I want to be alive with.” </blockquote>
  </b>
</i> <br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%209/AC4ED0E1-CFC1-4FCE-B276-A415E6ABBE2C_zpse5k8ownc.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1480070048i/21270616._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo AC4ED0E1-CFC1-4FCE-B276-A415E6ABBE2C_zpse5k8ownc.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1356294332" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3951422390514935037"><br/>*Roman's turn for 2015 favorite re-read!!!* :P<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Be careful," he says.<br/>"Why?" I’m not thinking about being careful. I’m thinking about one last push, of letting go, of flying, and of falling.<br/>“You aren’t allowed to die without me,” he whispers.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>*Indiscernible noise* Did you hear that? What’s that, you ask? That noise….what is that noise??? Let me tell you what that noise is: That’s the sound of <b>my heart beating</b>, <b>my soul</b> soaring, my <b>spirits</b> shining blindingly bright, my <b>fangirl</b> screeching…</span>
  <span id="freeText3951422390514935037" style="display:none"><br>*Roman's turn for 2015 favorite re-read!!!* :P<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Be careful," he says.<br>"Why?" I’m not thinking about being careful. I’m thinking about one last push, of letting go, of flying, and of falling.<br>“You aren’t allowed to die without me,” he whispers.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>*Indiscernible noise* Did you hear that? What’s that, you ask? That noise….what is that noise??? Let me tell you what that noise is: That’s the sound of <b>my heart beating</b>, <b>my soul</b> soaring, my <b>spirits</b> shining blindingly bright, my <b>fangirl</b> screeching….That, my lovely Goodread friends, is the sound of me falling head over heels in love with yet another book. <br><br>But no, hear me out. This isn’t simply <i>just a book</i>, this is <i>the</i> book that I have been staring at for months…MONTHS. <b>I don’t do sad books</b>, ya hear? Never. Nada. No way, Jose. I HATE SOBBING UNCONTROLLABLY for senseless sadness with no happy ending-Capiche? But for some reason…this book continued to call to me. I won’ t lie and say it has the best reviews ever-it doesn’t. I also won’t go so far as to say it has horrible reviews-it really, truly doesn’t. What we have here, folks, is a case of <b>what you are looking for in a book</b> and <b>what you are willing to accept in a book</b>. I guess…I guess I just didn’t know what I was looking for. When I saw this book, it was insta-love at it’s finest. Chelsea sees cover, Chelsea falls in love. Simple. Chelsea reads blurb? Chelsea falls in love….except for that teeny tiny detail, hmm, what was it? Oh yeah-this book centered around two suicidal teens. Yikes…Heavy much? <br><br><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>Depression is like a heaviness that you can’t ever escape. It crushes down on you, making even the smallest things like tying your shoes or chewing on toast seem like a twenty-mile hike uphill. Depression is a part of you; it’s in your bones and your blood. If I know anything about it, this is what I know: It’s impossible to escape.</b>
</blockquote><br><br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/large%208_zpsqyiyxak7.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1439904917ra/15901969.gif" alt=" photo large 8_zpsqyiyxak7.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><br>So what did I do next? I did what I always do: I researched <i>the shit</i> out of this book. But not before I hastily exited out of the browser once I saw ‘suicide pact.’ I will admit I’m a morbidly curious person, and I refuse to read sad, overly-hyped books simply because I don’t want to cry into my cheerios for the hell of it. I’ve never understood the people who can do that shit over and over again…I mean, fuck, don’t we have enough sadness in this world? Why put yourself through that? I still don’t get it-even now. And yet….After jumping out of the browsing history, I found myself relentlessly going back to this book every week or two-It was like clockwork. So, like a stupid cat, I let my curiosity get the best of me and I began my extensive (yet careful-I’ve mastered the art of being thorough in my research without spoiling MUAHAHA) research on whether this book was ‘Chelsea safe’. My head told me stay away, continually. <b>But my heart wanted more</b>. <br><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>I spend a lot of time wondering what dying feels like. What dying sounds like. If I’ll burst like those notes, let out my last cries of pain, and then go silent forever. Or maybe I’ll turn into a shadowy static that’s barely there, if you just listen hard enough. </b>
</blockquote><br><br><br>My point? After months and months and weeks and weeks of being a total poonanner about this book, I took the plunge-<b>I one clicked the sonuvabitch</b> and set a date to read it. I was nervous, admittedly, being the way I am about my book characters. Anyone who knows me, even a little, knows I find a deep, visceral connection with them-Almost always. And, even more so, I add new bbfs to my list like, well, books to my TBR pile. So, getting back to the point of me getting to the point-<b>I am so glad I listened to my heart</b>. <br><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>My whole face burns and my stomach clenches and unclenches like a fist. It’s not like I feel guilty-after all, it’s not my fault her son wants to kill himself. But I didn’t exactly want to meet his family. This is the soccer mom problem I was trying to avoid. Two strikes against FrozenRobot-a pet turtle and a loving mom. If I were pickier, I’d say he had too much baggage. But considering my situation, I’m in no position to be choosy.</b>
</blockquote><br><br><br>This book was something special to me. No, I don’t have a history with depression, nor do I really, truly know someone who suffers from it. You can call me out on this, that’s for sure. But I think there are so many books where people can cry ‘You don’t know anything about […] so how can you say this is good or bad or accurate?’ Well, I can’t-But what I <i>can</i> tell you is how <b>beautiful</b> it was. How the writing flowed seamlessly from page to page and pulled you in so deep you felt like you were wading in honey because it was so smooth and flawless and, shockingly….<b>sweet</b>. This book, this book I had avoided for months on end because I thought the darkness would swallow me whole, was sweet. <br><br><br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/giphy%2037_zpsggejqddx.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1439904917ra/15901970.gif" alt=" photo giphy 37_zpsggejqddx.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>And this is exactly why Roman didn’t want a flake. But he ended up with a flake. A grade-A flake. Though, it’s his fault. He’s the one who turned me into one. </b>
</blockquote><br><br><br>But how can that <i>be</i>, you ask?? This book is about two depressed teens who have a literal date set to commit suicide. And God do I know that it feels wrong to talk about this like its no big deal because ‘it’s just a book.’ No, it’s not like that to me. It’s a big deal-<b>Suicide is not a joke</b>. It’s not about fictionalizing a dark, heavy matter for the sake of making some money for a story, it’s not about shedding fake, positive light about something that families suffer from every day, and <b>it breaks my heart that people actually feel this way</b>. To feel like there is no way out, that the only answer for suffering is to end your life-I don’t take that shit lightly, and it kills me that people don’t find that help they need before it’s too late. But this is a book, and I guess if I had to say one thing about it…..it felt real. <b>It felt wholly authentic to me, and not once did I feel it was contrived or misplaced in it’s message</b>. It was dark, morbid, and relentless in the ultimate end result-they wanted to do this, and not a chapter went by without this reminder. But it was also so <b>full of hope</b>, <b>humor</b>, <b>longing</b>, and a desire for things to be different than they were/are. <br><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>All of a sudden, I realize what that shadowy something is. It’s joy. FrozenRobot loves basketball. He loves playing it. No matter how hard he tries to push that joy away, it’s there. I wonder if joy has potential energy. Or if there is potential energy that leads to joy, like a happiness serum that lingers in people’s stomachs and slowly bubbles up to create the sensation we know as happiness.</b>
</blockquote><br><br><br>And I think that is ultimately why this book called to me even as all the others repelled me-I’m not out to get some sick kick from these teenagers’ suffering. I felt the <b>hope</b> shining through all the darkness…and I saw that there was a possible happy ending for these two. Most of the books you see with this subject matter scream ‘You. Will. Cry.’ And, again, that’s not why I choose to read. I choose to read because <b>I want to escape reality</b> and find solace in the pages of something that I know nothing about, if only to expand my mind in ways I never dreamed possible. And that is the definition of this book for me-While I have never suffered from depression myself, I feel, if only a little bit, like I got a good, hard look into the mind of two young teens who <i>were</i> depressed…And now, just maybe, I’ll think twice before discarding these signs in the future. I felt a deep, visceral connection not only to Aysel, but to Roman, as well. These two were beyond words to me-<b>I loved</b> them for their beautiful, broken minds. <b>I cried</b> for their vulnerability and aches so deep that the pain was unbearable-but invisible to the eye. And <b>I hated them</b> for their selfishness-for not seeing the effect they were going to have on other people when they were gone. But, admittedly, I didn’t hate them-<b>not even a little bit, not even at all.</b> ;) (Eh? Eh? Name that moviiiie)<br><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>I guess he’s right: I am a flake. But maybe meeting Roman has helped me to understand myself better. Yes, I’m broken. And yes, he’s broken. But the more we talk about it, the more we share our sadness, the more I start to believe that there could be a chance to fix us, a chance that we could save each other.</b>
</blockquote><br><br><br>Now that I’ve lost the majority of you (Come back? Pleeeease?) I absolutely <u>have to</u> talk about these characters who touched my soul. Like Aysel, <b>the girl who had no one to turn to at her darkest hour</b>, who feared what she would become because of her father’s actions; the girl who walked through the hallways trying to dodge the whispering and murmurs and venomous accusations. This young girl who, despite what we are always taught…<b>saw no other way out</b>. Aysel was a dark person-and with that darkness was a humor that somehow managed to lighten her. Her mind, while toxic with her intentions, was a quirky minefield of intelligent musings about physics and classical music. While it was harsh at first to hear how bleak she was about what her life was leading to, I eventually found solace in her mind because she really and truly was an intelligent and accomplished girl who had <b>so much to live for</b>…Even if she couldn’t see it.<br><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>He’s no longer FrozenRobot, my suicide partner from the internet. He’s Roman, the boy who kissed me by the river and held me all night. To me, there’s a difference. A big difference.<br>He’s no longer the person I want to die with; he’s the person I want to be alive with.</b>
</blockquote><br><br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/tumblr_inline_n78k70tRMM1swiylm_zpsqip8k9uy.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1439904917ra/15901971.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_inline_n78k70tRMM1swiylm_zpsqip8k9uy.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>And then Roman-Aka <i>FrozenRobot</i>. Lmao, while the name probably isn’t supposed to be funny, Aysel’s quips about it inside her mind cracked me up from the moment we first see that name. But, seriously-My dear, tortured Roman. Roman was by far the darkest of the two-<b>The most serious</b>, the <b>most dedicated</b> to what was coming…the <b>most determined</b> to follow through….it was tragic. It feels weird and wrong to say I was obsessed with Roman but…I was. His pain and heartache were palpable from the moment we first meet him. But, even more than that, he wasn’t what you’d expect: <b>Popular</b>, <b>athletic</b>, and <b>smothered with love </b> from an overprotective mother. I just…I can’t. I can’t even. I adored him. I adored his story. I adored his personality, his kindness, his protectiveness of Aysel, and <b>his longing to know her</b>…even as the days before their pact wore down like sand in an hourglass.<br><br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/tumblr_mazh9mNhHh1r0ik5uo1_r1_500_zpsbmr6meoq.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1439904917ra/15901972.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_mazh9mNhHh1r0ik5uo1_r1_500_zpsbmr6meoq.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>I wonder if that’s how darkness wins, by convincing us to trap it inside ourselves, instead of emptying it out.</b>
</blockquote><br><br><br>People might even say I’m belittling the story’s message by saying how much I loved their romance-<b>
  <u>I don’t give a fuck</u>
</b>. This romance was heart-stopping, butterfly inducing, I-can’t-breathe-because-of-the-feels addicting…and I’m not ashamed nor embarrassed to tout that. I believe, despite the probably unpopular opinion, that the romance is what made them begin to heal-what gave them hope. <b>Hope that someone finally understood them</b>, understood the pain of what it feels like to be utterly crushed and like your soul was being sucked into a black vortex of nothingness every single day of your life. Romance doesn’t solve the whole world’s problems…but finding a friend who understands you, who loves you for who you are? I believe, in my heart of hearts, that this makes a <u>huge</u> difference in a person’s well-being-<u>depressed or not</u>. That’s <u>MY</u> opinion, and I wouldn’t change it for the world. <b>I adored them together</b>…<b>and I adored them separately</b>. Their message stirred something deep inside of me, and I won’t likely forget it for a long time. When Aysel starts to realize life just might be worth living….<b>will she be able to pull Roman off the ledge before it’s too late</b>?<br><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"You’re like a gray sky. You’re beautiful, even though you don’t want to be.”</b>
</blockquote><br><br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/tumblr_mp4evjgnKs1s96ia8o1_500_zpskdw5huyd.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1439906412ra/15902383.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_mp4evjgnKs1s96ia8o1_500_zpskdw5huyd.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>I’m not going to spoil their fates…that would be wrong of me. But I think it needs to be said that, not every book has to end in tragedy to make a big impact or for you to love it-and I know most people aren’t like that-like me, and my closest friends, for instance. But I must say, I see the best ratings popping up for tragic books. And let me ask you this….if that person hadn’t died or this or that hadn’t happened….<b>Would it still have been epic in your eyes</b>? Unforgettable? Astounding? I see this a lot and I just had to say that. <b>This book, whether tragic or not, was alluring and addicting from page one. </b> There was never a dull or boring moment, and the story never dragged. The writing flowed smoothly and the book was over in a blur-it was never a chore to finish this, even as the scary possibility of what was to come drew nearer. Quite the opposite, in fact. I literally, I kid you not, could. Not. Stop. Thinking. About. This. Book. It was midnight when I picked it up, and had to put it down at 50%-literally, I had to force myself-to savor the last 50%. I wasn’t even tired. I just couldn’t ruin what was possibly one of my favorite books this year by cramming it all into one late night sitting. <br><br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/tumblr_n6hghmR6pn1r4umbho1_500_zpscx6rmwzb.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1439904917ra/15901973.gif" alt=" photo tumblr_n6hghmR6pn1r4umbho1_500_zpscx6rmwzb.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>Everything used to seem so final, inevitable, predestined. But now I’m starting to believe that life may have more surprises in store than I ever realized. Maybe it’s all relative, not just light and time like Einstein theorized, but everything. Like life can seem awful and unfixable until the universe shifts a little and the observation point is altered, and then suddenly, everything seems more bearable.</b>
</blockquote><br><br><br>So, it’s all up to what you’re looking for, really. Me? I was looking for something to touch me on a deeper level, looking for something that made me <i>feel</i>-and not in the perilous kind of way, for once. I just wanted authentic, real characters who had actual problems….and I got it. I will never support the real act-It’s just my personal belief-but this book….it touched my heart in ways I never imagined possible. And for that, I will be eternally grateful. (Again, name that movviieee :P)<br><br><br><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/chelsea/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="200" width="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1491628712i/22430034._SX540_.jpg" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <u>
  <b></b>
</u><br><br><a title="Facebook" href="https://www.facebook.com/starcrossedbookblog" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438055977i/15660595.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a title="Twitter" href="https://twitter.com/starcrossedblog" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438055639i/15660580.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1806319614?book_show_action=true">Dec 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aj the Ravenous Reader" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader">Aj the Ravenous Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062391124" href="/book/show/23215484-my-heart-and-other-black-holes">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Aj the Ravenous Reader by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please">Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ </a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=mental-health">mental-health</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1806319614" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7160943627512769107"><br/><b>3.5 stars rounded up because it’s my last book review for 2016 ^^</b><br/><br/>It is my steadfast personal principle that my life is never mine to take and it’s why I try to avoid books on suicide as much as possible but I’ve heard a lot of good things about <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18336965.My_Heart_and_Other_Black_Holes' title='My Heart and Other Black Holes by Jasmine Warga' rel='nofollow noopener'>My Heart and Other Black Holes</a> and I got really intrigued with the idea on “suicide partners” so I took the plunge and I could now say that it was totally worth the risk. The two characters in the story make me empathize with their causes because they bel</span>
  <span id="freeText7160943627512769107" style="display:none"><br><b>3.5 stars rounded up because it’s my last book review for 2016 ^^</b><br><br>It is my steadfast personal principle that my life is never mine to take and it’s why I try to avoid books on suicide as much as possible but I’ve heard a lot of good things about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18336965.My_Heart_and_Other_Black_Holes" title="My Heart and Other Black Holes by Jasmine Warga" rel="nofollow noopener">My Heart and Other Black Holes</a> and I got really intrigued with the idea on “suicide partners” so I took the plunge and I could now say that it was totally worth the risk. The two characters in the story make me empathize with their causes because they believe there is no other better course in life than to end their own. <br><br>Although I think the story lacks better resolutions on several conflicts and that the turning point and conclusion sort of just happened in a nearly fairytale like fashion, I think this is a significantly unique debut novel about two people who met at the darkest times of their lives written in a very smart and witty manner that readers would enjoy despite the sad themes. I knew I had good reason to empathize with the characters because they do grow in the story. Although their resolve to end their lives is as stiff as an unwashed sock for three years, knowing each other brought a change to both their lives whether they acknowledge it or not and that simple change is really all it takes to make a difference. <br><br>I think many of our young people today heavily seek validation and acceptance from society- others even depend their lives on it. The story reminds us however how flimsy and unreliable it is to always seek other people’s approval to prove your self-worth when all you really need is the acceptance and love of the people you love and those who truly matter to you. The book also reminds that there are still many kindhearted people out there. It’s just sometimes we tend to think the worst of other people when often, many of them (even strangers) genuinely care. ;)<br><br>Happy early birthday,my lovely friend, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1356294332?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Chelsea</a>. I wish you a wonderful 2017 with your family. Here’s my baby Leo to render you a birthday dance number. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1478317734ra/21060086.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="7160943627512769107" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1806319614">

<div id="review_1254040864" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1254040864" />
    <a title="Kai" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41788524-kai"><img alt="Kai" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573562141p2/41788524.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1254040864?book_show_action=true">Apr 13, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kai" href="/user/show/41788524-kai">Kai</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=2016">2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1254040864" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6640999647328492509"><i>“You know, Zellie, there are enough broken things in the world. You shouldn't go around breaking things just for the fun of it.”</i><br/><br/>2 Stars<br/><br/>The fact that I don't remember even reading this book after finishing it just 4 months ago says everything.<br/><br/>This was not necessarily a bad book. Maybe I've already read too many similar books, but this felt like a beginner's guide to depression. A very important and very popular topic at the moment, but for me many of the lines in this novel felt staged. Predictab</span>
  <span id="freeText6640999647328492509" style="display:none"><i>“You know, Zellie, there are enough broken things in the world. You shouldn't go around breaking things just for the fun of it.”</i><br /><br />2 Stars<br /><br />The fact that I don't remember even reading this book after finishing it just 4 months ago says everything.<br /><br />This was not necessarily a bad book. Maybe I've already read too many similar books, but this felt like a beginner's guide to depression. A very important and very popular topic at the moment, but for me many of the lines in this novel felt staged. Predictability and unoriginality of plot as well as characters, made me feel like I had read this story many times before. Actually, I even played this story on stage just last year. In <i>Norway.Today</i> two strangers meet on an online platform for suicidals. They plan a trip to Norway, where they want to jump of a cliff.<br />In <i>My Heart and Other Blacke Holes</i> it may only be the Ohio River but let's not forget that the main characters also fall in love. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[And decide not to jump. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Loose Ends</b><br />Aysel (Uh-zell) has family and classmates, who try to reach out to her. While she ignores those attempts, I would've liked her to acknowledge them at some point. Especially her sisters would have deserved it.<br /><br /><b>Likeability</b><br />I couldn't warm up to neither Aysel nor Roman. They both had character traits that bothered me a lot. While she was rather self-centered and impolite, he got angry over her making jokes all the time.<br /><br />One look at the cover sums up my feelings for this book. Messy, rather grey-ish and a little dull.<br />But I think the author has lots of potential. I'm often disappointed by an author's debut work, but with more experience and time, their writing could improve. Jasmine Warga has the talent, so let's see what the future holds.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/fantasticbooksandwheretofindem/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6640999647328492509" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
