<div id="review_1505045571" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1505045571" />
    <a title="Rachel Reads Ravenously" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously"><img alt="Rachel Reads Ravenously" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539149211p2/14514998.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1505045571?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel Reads Ravenously" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel Reads Ravenously" href="/user/show/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously">Rachel Reads Ravenously</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062324672" href="/book/show/22328549-my-heart-and-other-black-holes">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=hardcover">hardcover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=library-checkout">library-checkout</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1505045571" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18121170779923312265"><b> 4 stars! </b><br/><br/><b> <i> “Maybe we all have darkness inside of us and some of us are better at dealing with it than others.” </i> </b><br/><br/><a href='http://s177.photobucket.com/user/dawnygirl07/media/My%20Heart%20and%20Other%20Black%20Holes%20casting.png.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452578786i/17709998._SX540_.png' alt=' photo My Heart and Other Black Holes casting.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Sixteen year old Aysel is ready to die. Thrown in the aftermath of her father’s actions, she has been shunned and pulled away from everyone close in her life. An outcast at school and in her own home, Aysel has been spending her time browsing suicide websites where she meets Roman. They make a pact to kill themselves on a specific day, and in order to keep up pretenses for their f</span>
  <span id="freeText18121170779923312265" style="display:none"><b> 4 stars! </b><br><br><b> <i> “Maybe we all have darkness inside of us and some of us are better at dealing with it than others.” </i> </b><br><br><a href="http://s177.photobucket.com/user/dawnygirl07/media/My%20Heart%20and%20Other%20Black%20Holes%20casting.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452578786i/17709998._SX540_.png" alt=" photo My Heart and Other Black Holes casting.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Sixteen year old Aysel is ready to die. Thrown in the aftermath of her father’s actions, she has been shunned and pulled away from everyone close in her life. An outcast at school and in her own home, Aysel has been spending her time browsing suicide websites where she meets Roman. They make a pact to kill themselves on a specific day, and in order to keep up pretenses for their families, they begin to spend time together. <br><br><a href="http://s177.photobucket.com/user/dawnygirl07/media/pagebreak.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421135336i/13327545.png" alt=" photo pagebreak.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b> <i> “You're like a grey sky. You're beautiful, even though you don't want to be.” </i> </b><br><br>I’m not normally one for the teen suicide genre, I find I cannot relate often times and cannot understand the desire to take one’s own life. Imagine my surprise when my heart just bled for Aysel and Roman and each of their situations. Aysel brought my eyes to tears multiple times in the beginning of this book. She was thrust into a horrible life situation very suddenly, the actions of her father ruining her life and the lives of others. She’s shunned by her classmates at school, and she stays away from those trying to be nice to her because she doesn’t want them hurt by association. Her family doesn’t know how to reach her, and at times it seems like they don’t want to.<br><br>Roman had an equally horrific reason for wanting to take his own life, one shrouded in guilt I couldn’t even begin to understand. As a romantic interest, he wasn’t my favorite because while he accepted Aysel and didn’t judge her, he also didn’t seem to have her best interests at heart. In fact he was a lot more invested in the pact than he was in a friendship with Aysel.<br><br><b> <i> “Depression is like a heaviness that you can’t ever escape. It crushes down on you, making even the smallest things like tying your shoes or chewing on toast seem like a twenty-mile hike uphill. Depression is a part of you; it’s in your bones and your blood.” </i> </b><br><br>I picked up this book and couldn’t put it back down. Reading this book you wouldn’t think this was a debut novel by this author. I honestly think her books will only continue to get better based on the great quality of this first book. Aysel was my favorite part of this book, I never at any point felt her feelings were unjustified, even if her turn around was fairly quick. This is a young adult novel that I feel will stand the test of time.<br><br><b> <i> “I will be stronger than my sadness.” </i> </b><br><br><a href="http://s177.photobucket.com/user/dawnygirl07/media/RRR.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444273756i/16478167._SX540_.png" alt=" photo RRR.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1268296272" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1268296272" />
    <a title="✦❋Arianna✦❋" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23370948-arianna"><img alt="✦❋Arianna✦❋" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420671997p2/23370948.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1268296272?book_show_action=true">Apr 30, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✦❋Arianna✦❋" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✦❋Arianna✦❋" href="/user/show/23370948-arianna">✦❋Arianna✦❋</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1268296272" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17080000946277951013"><b>3.5 Stars!!</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1432474776i/14969113.jpg' width='400' height='430' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>If you didn’t know depression is a common mental disorder, characterized by sadness, loss of interest or pleasure, feelings of guilt or low self-worth, disturbed sleep or appetite, feelings of tiredness, and poor concentration. It affects more than 121 million people worldwide. It is not uncommon for depressed individuals to have thoughts about suicide whether or not they really intend to act on these thoughts. <i>“My Heart and Other Black Holes”</i> is a book about depression, overcoming it</span>
  <span id="freeText17080000946277951013" style="display:none"><b>3.5 Stars!!</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1432474776i/14969113.jpg" width="400" height="430" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If you didn’t know depression is a common mental disorder, characterized by sadness, loss of interest or pleasure, feelings of guilt or low self-worth, disturbed sleep or appetite, feelings of tiredness, and poor concentration. It affects more than 121 million people worldwide. It is not uncommon for depressed individuals to have thoughts about suicide whether or not they really intend to act on these thoughts. <i>“My Heart and Other Black Holes”</i> is a book about depression, overcoming it, discovering yourself and ultimately finding something to live for. I haven’t read many books about this mental disorder, but I have to say this author did a great job describing how it is to be a teenager who struggles with this mental disorder.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“What people never understand is that depression isn’t about the outside; it’s about the inside. Something inside me is wrong. Sure, there are things in my life that make me feel alone, but nothing makes me feel more isolated and terrified than my own voice in my head.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>Our heroine is Aysel, a 16 years old girl who doesn’t want to live anymore. She suffers from depression, fantasizing about it and wondering what dying feels like. She feels guilty because her father is what he is and because of what he did. She feels humiliated, she’s lonely and she thinks the world would be better without her since she believes she will end up like her father. She doesn’t have friends, she’s not close with her mother or her step-siblings, never allowing anyone in. <br><br>Aysel decides she needs a suicide partner. On Smooth Passages, a website for people who wants to die she meets FrozenRobot aka Roman, a 17 years old boy who decides like Aysel to give up. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“...he looks like someone who was designed to be popular and successful, but he also looks like someone who was made to wear grief.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>Roman doesn’t look like someone who wants to kill himself, he has a loving family and he also has friends. He still has dreams, but he believes he doesn’t deserve to live. <br><br>As the story progresses Aysel and Roman plan how to kill themselves getting to know each other in the process. They become some sort of friends and maybe they would have become something more if the reality would have been different. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Maybe it’s all relative, not just light and time like Einstein theorized, but everything. Like life can seem awful and unfixable until the universe shifts a little and the observation point is altered, and then suddenly, everything seems more bearable.”<br></i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>Honestly this book was dark, sad and almost depressing. Like I mentioned before the author did a great job portraying Aysel’s character. She suffers from depression, but she’s a very likeable heroine and I loved her snarky personality. She felt real, her pain felt real and I’m sure many readers who suffered or still suffers from this mental disorder will relate with her. Roman is a character I liked, almost the entire time reading this novel. IMO he’s not as developed like Aysel's character and the way he is at times irritated me a little. I felt for him, I did, but at times he felt a little...selfish I guess.<br><br>I loved how easily the two of them interacted with each other. From the beginning I felt their connection and I enjoyed their dialogue for the most part. I also loves the philosophy/physics aspect of the story and all the classical music references. I found this aspects very refreshing and not only for a YA. <br><br>Even if the subject matter is tough and emotional, there’s some romance here. And I liked the romance aspect of the story. What I didn’t like was the idea that love can change everything and who you are. I didn’t buy it! It’s nice to think love conquers all or that love is the answer for everything, but let’s face it, is not very realistic. It goes without saying Aysel’s realization came too suddenly. From that point everything felt rushed. Also I wanted to know what happened with Aysel’s father or how ‘the talk’ between Aysel and her mother changed their relationship or if their family’s dynamic changed somehow. <br><br>And epilogue whould have been nice!<br><br>Overall, a great read!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17080000946277951013" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1268296272">

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1009120937" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1009120937" />
    <a title="Giselle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle"><img alt="Giselle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310159877p2/4800103.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1009120937?book_show_action=true">Jul 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Giselle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Giselle" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle">Giselle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062324672" href="/book/show/22328549-my-heart-and-other-black-holes">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1009120937" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9987106110810115205"><i>My Heart and Other Black Holes</i> delves into the lives of two suicidal teens who make a pact to be each other's suicide partner. Yes, this novel is messed up and sad and shocking at times to think that someone would want a sort of motivational coach to make sure they achieve death, but suicide pacts do happen, especially with teens, so no matter how effed up this is, it is real and all too heartbreaking. Still, this book is supposed to be an emotional mess, and it really should be considering the </span>
  <span id="freeText9987106110810115205" style="display:none"><i>My Heart and Other Black Holes</i> delves into the lives of two suicidal teens who make a pact to be each other's suicide partner. Yes, this novel is messed up and sad and shocking at times to think that someone would want a sort of motivational coach to make sure they achieve death, but suicide pacts do happen, especially with teens, so no matter how effed up this is, it is real and all too heartbreaking. Still, this book is supposed to be an emotional mess, and it really should be considering the subject matter and everything surrounding it, yet I found myself feeling a bit indifferent towards it all. <br><br>Suicide is a tough subject to execute in a novel, and while there are some realistic parts, the whole premise (which was basically a how-to on finding a suicide partner and then you add in the "love is the answer" bit..) made me fear for a troubled teen reading this book. I was even uncomfortable at times, especially when it came to the romance. You can't help but NOT want to root for the romance - because how mismatched is that? Like for instance, Roman would get upset about her maybe not coming through to their promise to kill themselves. He's supposed to be this character who we know will become a sort of love-interest from the start, and so we should like him, but he comes off as way too selfish! Sorry if you feel she maybe doesn't want to DIE anymore so you have to do it yourself! Poor you! Plus, the whole "love is a cure" idea is sweet and all, but it didn't work for me in this book. I felt as if Aysel's realization came on too suddenly, especially having been told that depression had been with her for a long time. I didn't see her climb out of the hole she was in, it was just like: <i>boom</i>, I'm not suicidal anymore because I'm in love! <br><br>Another aspect I disliked is how the "mysteries" are handled. Her dad is in jail for some major crime that happened. We know this is the reason she's been depressed, but we're only given hints of what exactly her dad did at first, making me believe there would be some kind of shocking reveal, here. But the reveal kind of fizzles out when it's unraveled fairly casually - and there's no twist, here, it's exactly what you easily assume it to be. The same could be said about FrozenRobot and his story. I feel like there was some lost potential in both cases. More-so, I felt like hints were dropped to grab our interest but were not really followed through. <br><br>With that out of the way, this novel is still beautifully written with sensitive topics that pull you in. I didn't find it as emotionally compelling as I expected it to be, but I do believe if the romance was not such a big part of her healing that I would have found myself connecting to it much more than I did. It seems like the majority of readers are finding it to be a much more emotional read than I did, so if you like these dark and difficult topics I do recommend you give this one a try. <br><br>--<br><i>An advance copy was provided by the publisher for review.</i><br><br>For more of my reviews, visit my blog at <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Xpresso Reads</a> <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1388702323i/7905232.png" width="380" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9987106110810115205" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_816698296" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/816698296" />
    <a title="Kayla" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3108455-kayla"><img alt="Kayla" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473956218p2/3108455.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/816698296?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kayla" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kayla" href="/user/show/3108455-kayla">Kayla</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer816698296" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2997189489572031338">Before reading MY HEART AND OTHER BLACK HOLES, I never expected that a book about a teen suicide pact could be so full of hope. And yet, that's exactly what I felt while reading it. Of course, it was the *heartbreaking* sort of hope, the kind where I grew to love Aysel and Roman, two characters who have so much passion and potential, yet direct that energy toward their mutual goal: helping each other die. <br/><br/>Watching Aysel and Roman get to know each other was such a good reminder that the way we se</span>
  <span id="freeText2997189489572031338" style="display:none">Before reading MY HEART AND OTHER BLACK HOLES, I never expected that a book about a teen suicide pact could be so full of hope. And yet, that's exactly what I felt while reading it. Of course, it was the *heartbreaking* sort of hope, the kind where I grew to love Aysel and Roman, two characters who have so much passion and potential, yet direct that energy toward their mutual goal: helping each other die. <br /><br />Watching Aysel and Roman get to know each other was such a good reminder that the way we see ourselves isn't always reliable. That we should be wary of letting guilt and shame become dark clouds we define ourselves by—because, for every dark cloud, there are silver linings of empathy, tenderness, a sense of humor, artistic talent, kindness toward animals, love, and so much more. That, sometimes, all it takes is a connection with someone who <i>gets</i> us to show us we're not as alone as we think we are. <br /><br />I think this will be an important book in the world because it has the potential to BE that connection for those who are reluctant to talk with an actual human about the dark clouds that haunt them—through Aysel and Roman, perhaps they will finally find someone to identify with. If this book shows just one person that their unique life is worth living, or takes the weight out of the burdens they carry, it will be a wonderful thing. I suspect, though, it will be a much-needed ray of light for far more than just one person.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2997189489572031338" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Swaroop Kanti" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Swaroop Kanti" href="/user/show/100264072-swaroop-kanti">Swaroop Kanti</a>

<div id="review_1103897419" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1103897419" />
    <a title="spencer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29377707-spencer"><img alt="spencer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605244321p2/29377707.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1103897419?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="spencer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="spencer" href="/user/show/29377707-spencer">spencer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062324672" href="/book/show/22328549-my-heart-and-other-black-holes">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29377707-spencer?shelf=2015-favorites">2015-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29377707-spencer?shelf=my-children">my-children</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1103897419" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11846640003885368033"><br/><br/><b>
  <i>“Depression is like a heaviness that you can’t ever escape. It crushes down on you, making even the smallest things like tying your shoes or chewing on toast seem like a twenty-mile hike uphill. Depression is a part of you; it’s in your bones and your blood.” </i>
</b><br/><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1415056175l/18336965.jpg' width='400' height='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>__________________________________<br/><br/>This book will get under your skin and live inside you. It is tragic, empowering (it has a few hopeful moments), and beautiful. I can not get enough of this book. It's truly incredible.<br/><br/><b>
  <u>1) The Plot</u>
</b><br/><br/>Si</span>
  <span id="freeText11846640003885368033" style="display:none"><br><br><b>
  <i>“Depression is like a heaviness that you can’t ever escape. It crushes down on you, making even the smallest things like tying your shoes or chewing on toast seem like a twenty-mile hike uphill. Depression is a part of you; it’s in your bones and your blood.” </i>
</b><br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1415056175l/18336965.jpg" width="400" height="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>__________________________________<br><br>This book will get under your skin and live inside you. It is tragic, empowering (it has a few hopeful moments), and beautiful. I can not get enough of this book. It's truly incredible.<br><br><b>
  <u>1) The Plot</u>
</b><br><br>Sixteen year old Aysel has been suffering depression ever since her father committed an awful crime. It's gotten to the point where the only way out of her sadness is to end it all. So, she decides she wants to commit suicide. She can't do it alone, so she finds a website dedicated to help people kill themselves and to find a person who's willing to kill themselves with Aysel. Whenever she finds Roman-the guy who is willing to kill himself with her-, they have nothing in common. But eventually their path becomes more concrete, and Aysel questions if she wants to actually do it.<br><br>So, just from the synopsis alone, one can tell that this is a serious book that deals with serious topics. This book is so dark, and it deals with mental-illness in a way that is incredibly truthful, and as someone who fights depression and has multiple suicide attempts, this book is insanely accurate. A lot of books have delved into mental illness, especially the topic of depression and suicide, just to name a few: <i>All the Bright Places</i> by Jennifer Niven (which I honestly didn't enjoy) and <i>I Was Here</i> by Gayle Forman (which I also didn't like). So, I was hesitant to see if this book would be like those two or if it could stand on its own, and it did. This book also made me cry in the last 100 pages or so multiple times. <br><br> <b>If you are struggling with suicidal urges, please tell someone immediately or call the National Suicide Prevention Hotline: 1 (800) 273-8255 I'm not going to say it gets better, but life <i>is</i> worth fighting for, and if you kill yourself, you'll never know what might have been.</b><br><br><b>
  <u>2) The Characters</u>
</b><br><br><b>Aysel</b> - She is one to the most incredible protagonists I've ever read from. Her whole story is heartbreaking, and she's just so lost, and you desperately want her to find herself.<br><br><b>Roman</b> - Likewise with Roman, he is incredibly broken after a dramatic event in his life. <br><br>Both of the characters are easy to relate to, especially if you're dealing with depression. <br><br>Their story broke my heart, and I am so eager to read anything else this woman writes.<br><br><b>
  <u>3) The Writing</u>
</b><br><br>- <i>“Sometimes I wonder if my heart is like a black hole--it's so dense that there's no room for light, but that doesn't mean it can't still suck me in.” </i><br><br>- <i>“It's like your sadness is so deep and overwhelming that you're worried it will drown everyone else in your life if you let them too close to it.”</i><br><br>- <i>"I bet if you cut open my stomach, the black slug of depression would slide out.” </i><br><br>- <i>“He was fucking sad. That's it. That's the point. He knows life is never going to get any different for him. That there's no fixing him. It's always going to be the same monotonous depressing bullshit. Boring, sad, boring, sad. He just wants it to be over.” </i><br><br><b>
  <u>4) Conclusion</u>
</b><br><br>This book changed me and how I see things.<br><br><i>★★★★★/5 Stars!!!!</i><br><br><br><br><br> <br><br><br><br><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="11846640003885368033" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2251380496" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2251380496" />
    <a title="Greta G" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45248887-greta-g"><img alt="Greta G" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525435609p2/45248887.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2251380496?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Greta G" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Greta G" href="/user/show/45248887-greta-g">Greta G</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45248887-greta-g?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45248887-greta-g?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45248887-greta-g?shelf=owned-in-english">owned-in-english</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2251380496" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer46991469492225544">This is a bittersweet story about two teenagers who are depressed, isolated and suicidal. They meet on a website and become partners in suicide. <br/>In addition to this, the story touches upon divorce, parental neglect, bullying, murder and mental illness. <br/><br/><i>Aysel</i> has to deal with the consequences of a terrible thing her father did, while <i>Roman</i> is crushed by guilt for causing a tragic accident. <br/>In the face of all these adversities, isolation, shame, depression and suicidal thoughts are unsurprising co</span>
  <span id="freeText46991469492225544" style="display:none">This is a bittersweet story about two teenagers who are depressed, isolated and suicidal. They meet on a website and become partners in suicide. <br />In addition to this, the story touches upon divorce, parental neglect, bullying, murder and mental illness. <br /><br /><i>Aysel</i> has to deal with the consequences of a terrible thing her father did, while <i>Roman</i> is crushed by guilt for causing a tragic accident. <br />In the face of all these adversities, isolation, shame, depression and suicidal thoughts are unsurprising corollaries. <br />They both feel their lives are ruined and they’re unworthy of love. <br /><br />In spite of all these unpleasant and sensitive topics, this rather well-written book was an engaging, easy read. <br />Although the author succeeded in describing the sadness and pain of her two young characters accurately for the most part of the book, I couldn’t feel their torment. The book only left me feeling underwhelmed and conflicted about my own lack of compassion in the face of so much tragedy and unhappiness.<br /><br />The tone of the book was set early on : <br /><i>“There’s something poetic about the fact that the first boy to ever ask for my number is the same boy I’m going to die with.”</i> <br />From that point on, the novel became sentimentally predictable to me. Nevertheless I didn’t stop hoping for a realistic, satisfying ending, but what I got was a melodramatic one. </span>
  <a data-text-id="46991469492225544" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1589971718" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1589971718" />
    <a title="Warda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30036082-warda"><img alt="Warda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593385153p2/30036082.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1589971718?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Warda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Warda" href="/user/show/30036082-warda">Warda</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/24673330-my-heart-and-other-black-holes">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30036082-warda?shelf=mental-health">mental-health</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30036082-warda?shelf=i-fell-in-love">i-fell-in-love</a>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1589971718" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6838874444786627845">Wow, was not expecting for this book to have hit me as hard as it did. <br/><br/>First of all, trigger warnings for suicide. <br/><br/><b>MINOR SPOILERS AHEAD</b><br/><br/>Secondly, this is a tragic, heavy, but beautiful story about Aysel and Roman who have been affected by a loss of a loved one. For Aysel, it was her father who was imprisoned due to killing someone. Roman lost his younger sister due to a tragic accident that he blames himself for. Strangely, they both blame themselves for those incidents. Subsequently, they meet o</span>
  <span id="freeText6838874444786627845" style="display:none">Wow, was not expecting for this book to have hit me as hard as it did. <br /><br />First of all, trigger warnings for suicide. <br /><br /><b>MINOR SPOILERS AHEAD</b><br /><br />Secondly, this is a tragic, heavy, but beautiful story about Aysel and Roman who have been affected by a loss of a loved one. For Aysel, it was her father who was imprisoned due to killing someone. Roman lost his younger sister due to a tragic accident that he blames himself for. Strangely, they both blame themselves for those incidents. Subsequently, they meet on a website where one looks for a suicide partner. They meet and agree on a date. As the date of their planned suicide gets closer, things begin to change. <br /><br />Now, I know a lot of people hate this 'trope' of love making it better and I can't speak for clinical depression fully either (or suicide), though I went through something myself. But, love doesn't make the depression and the suicidal thoughts go away in this instance. They're acknowledged as something that will be constant. <br /><br />However, this is a personal story to the author. I appreciated how she explored depression and suicide. How she highlighted that this constant feeling of sadness isn't beautiful, neither does it make anyone interesting. But, it becomes a way for both characters to connect. To finally be understood and TALK to someone about what they've been facing. Their personal darkness. And feel a spark of hope, and coming to their own conclusion that they might not be how they see themselves, giving them the encouragement to see life slightly differently. To look for help and confide in their families. That the battle of depression most likely will never end, but that life might not be so bad after all. <br /><br />I cried a few times. There were just some moments that I could fully relate to and that I needed to read. I appreciated that this book included resources that others could use who battle depression and have suicidial thoughts. <br /><br />Just a beautiful, enlightening read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6838874444786627845" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1436277836" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1436277836" />
    <a title="Emer (A Little Haze)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4629647-emer-a-little-haze"><img alt="Emer (A Little Haze)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589390599p2/4629647.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1436277836?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emer (A Little Haze)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emer (A Little Haze)" href="/user/show/4629647-emer-a-little-haze">Emer (A Little Haze)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781444791532" href="/book/show/23301770-my-heart-and-other-black-holes">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=1star">1star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=abn-readalongs">abn-readalongs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=the-hype-lies">the-hype-lies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=read2016">read2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1436277836" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8274996129392423946"><i>
  <blockquote>"Music, especially classical music, ... has kinetic energy. ...once the notes are in the air, they collide against one another. They spark. They burst. <br/>I spend a lot of time wondering what dying feels like. What dying sounds like. If I'll burst like those notes, let out my last cries of pain, and then go silent forever. Or maybe I'll turn into a shadowy static that's barely there, if you just listen hard enough."</blockquote>
</i> <br/><br/><br/>You know when a woman says that she or something is fine then it really means t</span>
  <span id="freeText8274996129392423946" style="display:none"><i>
  <blockquote>"Music, especially classical music, ... has kinetic energy. ...once the notes are in the air, they collide against one another. They spark. They burst. <br />I spend a lot of time wondering what dying feels like. What dying sounds like. If I'll burst like those notes, let out my last cries of pain, and then go silent forever. Or maybe I'll turn into a shadowy static that's barely there, if you just listen hard enough."</blockquote>
</i> <br /><br /><br />You know when a woman says that she or something is fine then it really means trouble? Yeah??? Well this book was <i>fine</i>!<br /><br /><br /><b>OUCH!!!</b><br /><br /><br />Aysel was a teenage girl suffering with depression. Her father had committed a terrible crime and she felt like a pariah. In fact she turned her best friend away from her because she thought it was showing kindness to her by saving her from being associated with Aysel. Her mother had remarried and Aysel had a half-sister and -brother. But Aysel never felt like she belonged with them. Her sadness was ever present. She would describe it as a black slug living inside her. It ate her alive, consumed her whole being until she could not take it any more and decided that she wanted to die. And when we meet Aysel at the beginning of the book she has determined that she needs someone to be there with her in those last moments and so she seeks out a suicide companion. Enter Roman...<br /><br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>"The walls of our old frame house are thin, and I can hear Mom and Georgia rattling around in the kitchen. I imagine them hugging. Georgia wrapping her arms around Mom's thin waist and Mom running her fingers through Georgia's shiny ponytail. The two of them fitting, interlocking, like mothers and daughters are supposed to. Fitting in a way that I never have. My edges have always been too sharp, my grooves too deep.<br />That's what they should write on my tombstone: Aysel Leyla Seran, the Girl Who Never Fit."</blockquote>
</i> <br /><br /><br />Okay! So there wasn't really anything terribly wrong with this story. It was sweet, it was lovely. We had two very nice main characters. Neither were too annoying so applause all around!!! I particularly liked all the cute little references to school physics. There were some lovely ideas relating kinetic and potential energies to living and dying. Aysel queried what happened to all that potential energy of a body when death occurs. It was nice to see a YA book bring a little physics and basic thermodynamics into the fold with questions arising from the law of the conservation of energy (that's the one that states that energy cannot be created or destroyed but can be converted from one form to another). <br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>"Does a dead body still have potential energy or does it get transferred into something else? Can potential energy just evaporate into nothingness? That's the question I don't know the answer to. That's the question that haunts me."</blockquote>
</i> <br /><br />However, I never truly emotionally connected to the characters unfortunately. There was always something missing. At the time I questioned was it because the information as to what crime Aysel's father committed was held from us and used as a <i>dangling carrot</i> sort of plot device. Without that information early on it was just difficult to fully grasp the reasons why Aysel was so unhappy... But on hindsight I'm not sure that this was the case. I felt sorry for Aysel because it's a natural human emotion to feel that way when you read about someone else in pain. But I got the sense that this was a case of 'backwards' <i>show and tell</i>. We were told Aysel was sad but I needed to be shown the why. I needed to see more of her soul.... Gosh that sounds kind of creepy on my part YIKES!!!<br /><br /><br />But anyway for two thirds of the book I kept thinking that this was a nice, contemporary YA read and okay, I wasn't really emotionally connecting to the book but I was enjoying it so I was not displeased that I was reading it! Three stars was beckoning on the horizon. And I was feeling generally good about life. <br />Note, not <i>fine</i> but good!!! Yaaaaayyyy <b>*cheers*</b><br /><br /><br />Oh but then there was that final third and <b>oh what a mess!!!!</b><br />This is a book about depression. Please don't trivialise such a serious illness!!! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[There isn't an overnight magic cure and waiting for true love's kiss to take you out of your black little hole does not proper sense make. Sorry, guess I didn't realise I was reading a reimagined fairytale!!!!!! <b>*not amused face*</b><br /><br /><br />I fully appreciate what the author was trying to achieve. <br />Absolutely. <br />She wanted hope.<br />Light.<br />Good triumphing over evil and all that jazz. <br />If you are suffering from depression you want to believe there is hope. And you know what? There is. There is always hope. Suddenly things in your life can change, I truly want to believe that and do believe that. And you can meet someone who helps you by talking and seeing things through another perspective, or maybe you seek medical help and someone shines that light for you, or you can even read a book that rocks your world.... <br />Things <b>do</b> change, and sometimes in the most simplest and surprising of ways, and life truly can and <b>does</b> get better. So the same aim could have been achieved but... That quickly??? That drastically???<br /><br /><br />This book was so unrealistic in this last third in the manner of how things came about!! <br />Bye bye contemporary fiction and hello fantasy la-la land with rainbows and unicorns and endless summer days!!! <b>*sighs*</b><br />For Aysel to suddenly change her mind about wanting to live and not die because she fell in love with Roman and how he truly saw her... <b>*eye roll*</b><br />Yes this was very sweet. Very romantic. <br />But could she not have changed these same things about her views through I don't know... Eh friendship??? God forbid that we not always involve hormones... <b>*sigh*</b> <br />Or maybe she could have changed through a deeper understanding with her sister??? There was great potential in that aspect of the story. Two half-sisters, polar opposites. One with a happy, well adjusted Dad and the other without that safe sense of home. Such potential for connection...<br />Why does everything have to be because of romantic love?? Can we only truly want to live because we fall in love and meet our other half??? Because a knight in shining armour comes along and sees us so differently to how we see ourselves?? <b>NONSENSE!!!</b> C'mon authors! There are so many variations of love out there, it doesn't always have to be about that butterfly feeling!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />And so I had to dock a whole star off my rating because of my issues with the unrealistic setup of the last third of this book. I'm sorry! I know I wanted to experience some emotions because of reading this book... <br />Yeah...<br />Anger wasn't the one I was going for!!! <b>*furrowed brow*</b><br /><br /><br />And another thing! I was at appointments this past week where I had to sit in waiting rooms for extended periods of time and yet I chose not to bring this book with me because I thought I would bawl... (And who wants to see a grown woman do that in public!!! #awkward) But not even a tiny glisten of a tear did I shed either... <br /><b>DRY BARREN DESOLATE TEAR DUCTS!!!</b><br />Eh hellooooooooo?????????????? If you want someone to cry at your book then <b>I</b> am your <b>go-to-girl!!!</b> I always cry. <b>ALWAYS!!!</b> It's common knowledge. I will cry at just about anything. And you would have thought that there would be tears because of the emotive subject matter right????? Well not this time apparently!!! Sheesh.... I'm fine. <b>FINE!!!</b><br /><br /><br />Okay in summation, I didn't hate this book... but I didn't love it either. It landed somewhere in the awkward middle; just not middle enough that I could award it three stars. There are other YA books out there that handle the topic of depression and suicide in a much better and more realistic manner in my opinion. <br /><br /><br /><b>two stars</b><br /><br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>"Maybe it's all relative, not just light and time like Einstein theorised, but everything. Like life can seem awful and unfixable until the universe shifts a little and the observation point is altered, and then suddenly, everything seems more bearable."</blockquote>
</i><br /><br /><br /><b>one year later</b><br /><br />Lowering my rating because the memory of this book offends me. Not to mention the handling of mental illness and its "cure".....<br />*shudders*<br /><b>one star</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="8274996129392423946" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_920600599" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/920600599" />
    <a title="Danielle (Love at First Page)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1312450-danielle-love-at-first-page"><img alt="Danielle (Love at First Page)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578285312p2/1312450.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/920600599?book_show_action=true">Apr 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Danielle (Love at First Page)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Danielle (Love at First Page)" href="/user/show/1312450-danielle-love-at-first-page">Danielle (Love at First Page)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062324672" href="/book/show/22328549-my-heart-and-other-black-holes">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1312450-danielle-love-at-first-page?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1312450-danielle-love-at-first-page?shelf=cover-love">cover-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1312450-danielle-love-at-first-page?shelf=my-face-is-wet">my-face-is-wet</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1312450-danielle-love-at-first-page?shelf=pretty-writing">pretty-writing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1312450-danielle-love-at-first-page?shelf=genre-young-adult">genre-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1312450-danielle-love-at-first-page?shelf=favorites-young-adult">favorites-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1312450-danielle-love-at-first-page?shelf=own-kindle-book">own-kindle-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1312450-danielle-love-at-first-page?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer920600599" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15088294917268682048"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>I wonder if that's how darkness wins, by convincing us to trap it inside ourselves, instead of emptying it out.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><i>Wow.</i> What a powerful and painful and beautiful book, though not at all in the way I was expecting. This book pretty much snuck up on me. It's normally not a "me" book anyway (depressing subject matter = Danielle runs for the hills), and halfway through I wasn't sure where it was going. It's actually quite funny thanks to a snarky narrator, but it seemed almost aimless. Somew</span>
  <span id="freeText15088294917268682048" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>I wonder if that's how darkness wins, by convincing us to trap it inside ourselves, instead of emptying it out.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><i>Wow.</i> What a powerful and painful and beautiful book, though not at all in the way I was expecting. This book pretty much snuck up on me. It's normally not a "me" book anyway (depressing subject matter = Danielle runs for the hills), and halfway through I wasn't sure where it was going. It's actually quite funny thanks to a snarky narrator, but it seemed almost aimless. Somewhere along the way, though, it pulled me into its orbit. It happened so subtly and gradually that I was almost suprised when tears were tracking down my cheeks. Now <i>that's</i> what I call a meaningful reading experience.<br /><br />I think, for me, I expected Jasmine Warga's debut to be very difficult to read and sad and <i>heavy</i>, from beginning to end. Like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16151178.The_Sea_of_Tranquility" title="The Sea of Tranquility by Katja Millay" rel="nofollow noopener">The Sea of Tranquility</a>. So when that didn't happen, I had to recalibrate my expectations. Now having read it all the way through, I'm grateful that such a heavy subject matter was treated with sensitivity and frankness, but not in a way that made it hard for me to concentrate on anything but that aching feeling and a sense of dread. The heart and soul of this book are its characters, and I ended up caring for them so much. I could see the black holes they had fallen into, but I could see the light for them too, and I was hoping they'd find it. Don't get me wrong, Asyel and Roman's stories aren't anything but painful; Roman's especially killed me. And in no way is depression romanticized or trivialized. It's a very real issue that the book treats with all seriousness. There's just more that both characters realize they can give and fight for. I never felt like all hope was lost, which I greatly needed.<br /><br />The book begins with two teenagers meeting because they agree to be suicide partners. Asyel (her name rhymes with gazelle) and Roman are suffering for very different reasons, but their pain looks the same. For this reason the bond that forms between them is both genuine and intimate. It was almost strange for me, because I knew they were still planning to commit suicide together, but I loved seeing their relationship develop. It's not like they get along all that perfectly, but they clearly start to care about each other. Their interactions have a sweetness to them; soft, unexpected touches and quiet confessions and acceptance. Maybe this is a little bit of "love is a cure", but it was believable to me. There is no instant healing or answers, but slowly the blackness starts to leak out of them and love is what's left. I think what makes these characters so special to me is their togetherness, the way each sees the other, if that makes any sense. It's not always an easy romance to accept, but romantic and believable to me.<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>And maybe that's why I haven't told him. Not because I'm scared that he won't want to die with me anymore, but because I'm terrified that he'll still want me to die. That he'll agree that I should die.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />The writing itself is beautiful throughout, but it's in the second half when the book truly won me over. Asyel's character growth is just stunning. I already loved her snark and frank viewpoint, and her obsession with theoretical physics is quirky and endearing. When she begins to see things differently and want different things for herself, it feels natural and not sudden. I really believed she was crawling out of her black hole. Roman, however, scared the hell out of me. If I hadn't already peeked at the ending, I wouldn't know which way this book was going to go. We get glimpses of the boy he used to be - and still maybe is or could be - and his constant hand holding and half smiles made me all gooey - but he's still so empty on the inside. My heart broke for him; I doubt anyone will be able to not suffer with Roman for his loss. <br /><br />If you're thinking this story may not be for you because of the subject matter, I sincerely hope you'll reconsider. <i>My Heart and Other Black Holes</i> is morbid and painful - and so important of a message - but it's also hopeful and wonderfully told. Asyel and Roman are two characters who will stay with me for a good long while. Maybe death is what brings them together, but they needed each other for so much more.<br /><br />This review can also be found at <a href="http://www.loveatfirstpage.org/2015/03/05/review-my-heart-and-other-black-holes/" rel="nofollow noopener">Love at First Page</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15088294917268682048" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1666545313?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Adita ✨The Slumbering Insomniac✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Adita ✨The Slumbering Insomniac✨" href="/user/show/37265034-adita-the-slumbering-insomniac">Adita ✨The Slumbering Insomniac✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Physics and YA fans(both in one)</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Adita ✨The Slumbering Insomniac✨ by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/4629647-emer-a-little-haze">Emer (A Little Haze)</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37265034-adita-the-slumbering-insomniac?shelf=2016-reads">2016-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37265034-adita-the-slumbering-insomniac?shelf=page-turner">page-turner</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37265034-adita-the-slumbering-insomniac?shelf=ibooks">ibooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37265034-adita-the-slumbering-insomniac?shelf=ya-mania">ya-mania</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1666545313" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10160709024571490728">★★★★★★★★☆☆[8/10]<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465752365i/19396722._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>⏩Three things that made me want to pick this book from the three score books I had managed to adorn my library with, in the recent major-bookhaul. <br/><br/><b>
  <blockquote>“This must be a sign from the universe-if the only time you get lucky is when you're planning your suicide, it's definitely time to go.”</blockquote>
</b><br/><br/>✅<i>
  <u>
    <b>PHYSICS</b>
  </u>
</i>. (Notice that it is underlined and italicised and emboldened.) <br/>There is a good deal of Physics stuff in the story and I was surprised to find how easy Einstein's Relativity the</span>
  <span id="freeText10160709024571490728" style="display:none">★★★★★★★★☆☆[8/10]<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465752365i/19396722._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>⏩Three things that made me want to pick this book from the three score books I had managed to adorn my library with, in the recent major-bookhaul. <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“This must be a sign from the universe-if the only time you get lucky is when you're planning your suicide, it's definitely time to go.”</blockquote>
</b><br><br>✅<i>
  <u>
    <b>PHYSICS</b>
  </u>
</i>. (Notice that it is underlined and italicised and emboldened.) <br>There is a good deal of Physics stuff in the story and I was surprised to find how easy Einstein's Relativity theories were to get by, while I had been unnecessarily slogging at it for years. <i>
  <b>Aysel (read as uh-ZELL) Seran</b>
</i> is the kickass heroine, though in her own way- that is, if you can make peace with the fact that I consider 'I can't wait for the lecture on Paradise Lost to be over soon so that I can go grab a spot in the front in the Physics class' kind of kickassery to be über cool. <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“The only class I really like is physics. I'm no science genius, but this is the one class that I think may have some answers to my questions. Ever since I was little, I've been fascinated by the way things work. I used to take apart my toys, studying how all the little pieces fit together.”</blockquote>
</b><br><br>✅<i>
  <u>
    <b>SUICIDAL TEENAGERS.</b>
  </u>
</i> (Again?? ugh!!)<br>Aysel is trying to find a suicide partner. And, she meets <i>
  <b>FrozenRobot aka Roman Franklin</b>
</i>(a cutie, obviously).<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“I'm a little weirded out that FrozenRobot aka Roman wants to meet in such a public place. I guess that means he's not a serial killer or rapist or anything. Then again, I'm not sure it'd be so bad if he was a serial killer. At least I'd get it over with quickly.”</blockquote>
</b><br><br>Do they die? I am planning on launching a massive campaign against all those authors who take our pliable hearts for granted and throw grenades at them and expect them to hold up. <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“As the sun glints off the polished wooden court, I wonder what my classmates are going to do with all their hate and anger and fear once they don't have me here anymore.<br><br> I can't wait until they don't have me here anymore.”</blockquote>
</b><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[✅<i><u><b>HAPPY ENDING.</b></u></i><br>Thankfully, I don't have to. For a minute, I am going to stop thinking about how every time I have to feel heartbroken and instead focus on the grittiness of the issue. To quote the author, this story ends on a hopeful note. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Going by the golden rule that the authors don't write about depressing stuff unless there is a pressing need to bring our attention to that particular stuff, I decide to overlook the nimiety of suicide themed stories in the YA world- <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18460392.All_the_Bright_Places" title="All the Bright Places by Jennifer Niven" rel="nofollow noopener">All the Bright Places</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1217100.Thirteen_Reasons_Why" title="Thirteen Reasons Why by Jay Asher" rel="nofollow noopener">Thirteen Reasons Why</a>, for instance. Authors, even though they romanticise the notion of suicides in the books, in their attempts to portray the exact opposite picture, are constantly trying to make us see the ugly truths of the real world, harbouring the hope that their words will make at least an iota of difference in a person's life somewhere. I hope they succeed in their endeavours...<br><br><b>Because there is a bit of good everywhere and in everything, innit?</b><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“I once read in my physics book that the universe begs to be observed, that energy travels and transfers when people pay attention. Maybe that's what love really boils down to-having someone who cares enough to pay attention so that you're encouraged to travel and transfer, to make your potential energy spark into kinetic energy. Maybe all anyone ever needs is for someone to notice them, to observe them.”</blockquote>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465752365i/19396723.jpg" width="300" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="10160709024571490728" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1241960755" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1241960755" />
    <a title="BookOwl BookOwl" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32538757-bookowl-bookowl"><img alt="BookOwl BookOwl" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1474482520p2/32538757.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1241960755?book_show_action=true">Mar 31, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="BookOwl BookOwl" class="user" itemprop="url" name="BookOwl BookOwl" href="/user/show/32538757-bookowl-bookowl">BookOwl BookOwl</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32538757-bookowl-bookowl?shelf=i-cried">i-cried</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32538757-bookowl-bookowl?shelf=must-read">must-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32538757-bookowl-bookowl?shelf=recommend">recommend</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32538757-bookowl-bookowl?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32538757-bookowl-bookowl?shelf=serious-issues">serious-issues</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32538757-bookowl-bookowl?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32538757-bookowl-bookowl?shelf=unforgettable">unforgettable</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1241960755&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1241960755" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4321038547648971345">★★★★<br/><br/>" Depression is like a heaviness that you can’t ever escape. It crushes down on you, making even the smallest things like tying your shoes or chewing on toast seem like a twenty-mile hike uphill. Depression is a part of you; it’s in your bones and your blood. If I know anything about it, this is what I know: It’s impossible to escape. "<br/><br/>This is beyond true. <br/><br/>I for one suffered with depression from I was seven, straight through high school and college where it grew to an alarming and frightenin</span>
  <span id="freeText4321038547648971345" style="display:none">★★★★<br /><br />" Depression is like a heaviness that you can’t ever escape. It crushes down on you, making even the smallest things like tying your shoes or chewing on toast seem like a twenty-mile hike uphill. Depression is a part of you; it’s in your bones and your blood. If I know anything about it, this is what I know: It’s impossible to escape. "<br /><br />This is beyond true. <br /><br />I for one suffered with depression from I was seven, straight through high school and college where it grew to an alarming and frightening state. I can remember watching cars zip by and willing myself to just step in the road and be done with it all. Yes, it was that bad.<br /><br />I despised myself so bad, like I couldn't stand to look at myself in the mirror because all I could see staring back were all the flaws everyone; especially family members, would point out. <br /><br />I was too dark, my eyes were too big, I looked too much like my mother and I was going to be a failure like her, I was stupid and it goes on and on. . . <br /><br />Those were some painful times and frankly it drove me to the brink. But I saved myself. I found that the less I cared about what people thought about me and the more I accepted who I was, then the less painful these comments would be. It was all about self acceptance and self love, and so I was on my way to being happy.<br /><br />____________________________________<br /><br />What I loved about this was that it hit home, it brought back memories because I too was criticized and disliked because of my mother. And for what because she was stupid/brave enough to have me and everyday I would be reminded by this. <br /><br />Yeah people suck, especially those closest to you. And to imagine poor Aysel, who had it worse. It was real terrible what her father did but it was even worse what happened to her. How everyone directed their hate and fears towards a young girl who didn't do anything except have the genes of the man who killed a 'superstar'. (Yeah people really suck!)<br /><br />It was really hard reading this because I hate crying. I really do. And at the beginning of this novel that's all I did, but towards the end I saw where Aysel started to change (thanks to Roman). She began actually looking forward to her future, something a few weeks before was foreign to her, and as she grew happy so did I.<br /><br />I'm just really glad she turned out to be a flake.<br /><br />This book rocks! You should read it, even though it's a tad depressing it's totally worth it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4321038547648971345" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1467285168" />
    <a title="Sara (sarawithoutanH)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7397330-sara-sarawithoutanh"><img alt="Sara (sarawithoutanH)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545592752p2/7397330.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1467285168?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara (sarawithoutanH)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara (sarawithoutanH)" href="/user/show/7397330-sara-sarawithoutanh">Sara (sarawithoutanH)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780062324672" href="/book/show/22328549-my-heart-and-other-black-holes">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7397330-sara-sarawithoutanh?shelf=2016">2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1467285168" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16226552666618793342">I really liked Aysel as a narrator but ultimately I had issues with this book. I keep changing this review because the more I think about this book, the more I don't like it. I'll list them below in a spoiler section.<br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[I'm not an expert on depression, but I felt like the ending was a bit happy-go-lucky for what the tone had been earlier in the book. I thought the resolution was very sudden and every problem in the book seemed to right itself magically. It was a solid book for me up </span></span>
  <span id="freeText16226552666618793342" style="display:none">I really liked Aysel as a narrator but ultimately I had issues with this book. I keep changing this review because the more I think about this book, the more I don't like it. I'll list them below in a spoiler section.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I'm not an expert on depression, but I felt like the ending was a bit happy-go-lucky for what the tone had been earlier in the book. I thought the resolution was very sudden and every problem in the book seemed to right itself magically. It was a solid book for me up until the last 50 pages or so. It just didn't ring true to me as an ending. It seemed like a switch went off and then everyone was just happy again. A romantic relationship can't just solve your depression. I think the ending sort of trivialized how hard it is to get over depression, especially for a character like Aysel who had been struggling with it for years.<br /><br />I also didn't like how the characters both had extremely terrible backstories. I don't have an issue with the backstories themselves, more that they implied you have to have some terrible reason as to why you're depressed.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> </span>
